                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَأَلَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> (S, M, K) with <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign> following it, and <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَهُ عَنْ كَذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِكَذَا</foreign>, (S, * K,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَسْأَلُ</foreign>, (M,) <pb n="1283"/> inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سُؤَالٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسْأَلَةٌ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) which latter is also pronounced <foreign lang="ar">مَسَلَةٌ</foreign>, without the hemzeh, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَسْآلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَآلَةٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَةٌ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">سَأْلَةٌ</foreign>, (accord. to different copies of the K, the former of these two accord. to the TA, [and it appears from a statement that will be found below, voce <foreign lang="ar">سُؤْلٌ</foreign>, that one of these is correct, but in an excel-lent copy of the M, in the place thereof, I find, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18578-1" target="سَآءَلَهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n18579"/></foreign>, as a verb, doubly trans., first thus by itself, and secondly by means of <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ</foreign>, as shown by an ex. in a verse cited below, (see 3,) and this also is correct,]) all [sometimes] signify the same, (S, * K,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">He asked him such a thing;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">asked him, interrogated him, questioned him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inquired of him, respecting such a thing:</hi> but <foreign lang="ar">عن كذا</foreign> is more common than <foreign lang="ar">بكذا</foreign>: when <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَ</foreign> means the asking, or demanding, of property, it is trans. [only] by itself or by means of <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> [so that you say <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَهُ كَذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَ مِنْهُ كَذَا</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">he asked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demanded, of him such a thing</hi>]: (Er-Rághib, TA:) and one says also <foreign lang="ar">سَالَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَسَالُ</foreign>, (Akh, S, M, Msb, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">خَافَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَخَافُ</foreign>; (Msb, K;) which is of the dial. of Hudheyl; the medial letter of this being originally <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>, as is shown by the phrase, mentioned by AZ, <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا يَتَسَاوَلَانِ</foreign>: (TA:) [respecting this dial. var., see what follows:] the imperative (S, Msb, K, TA;) of <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَ</foreign> (S, Msb, TA) is <foreign lang="ar">اِسْأَلْ</foreign>; (S, M, Msb, K, TA;) and (S, K, &amp;c.) that of <foreign lang="ar">سَالَ</foreign>, (S, Msb, TA,) <foreign lang="ar">سَلْ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K, TA,) dual. <foreign lang="ar">سَلَا</foreign>, and pl. <foreign lang="ar">سَلُوا</foreign>, [these two being] irregular; (Msb;) and AAF mentions that Aboo-'Othmán heard one say <foreign lang="ar">اِسَلْ</foreign>, [a form omitted in some copies of the K, but mentioned in the CK,] meaning <foreign lang="ar">اِسْأَلْ</foreign>, suppressing the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign>, and transferring its vowel to the preceding letter, like as some of the Arabs said <foreign lang="ar">لَحْمَرُ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">الأَحْمَرُ</foreign> [as many do in the present day]: (M:) accord. to ISd, (TA,) the Arabs universally suppress the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> in the imperative except when they prefix to it <foreign lang="ar">فَ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">وَ</foreign>; (M, TA;) saying <foreign lang="ar">فَٱسْأَلْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَٱسْأَلْ</foreign>: (TA:) or when <foreign lang="ar">وَ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">فَ</foreign>] is prefixed, it is allowable to pronounce the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> and also to suppress it, as in saying <foreign lang="ar">وَٱسْأَلُوا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَسَلُوا</foreign>: (Msb:) and for the pass. <foreign lang="ar">سُئِلَ</foreign>, one may say <foreign lang="ar">سِيلَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">سُيِلَ</foreign>, in this instance making the kesreh to partake of the sound of dammeh, and <foreign lang="ar">سُولَ</foreign>; and also <foreign lang="ar">سُيِلَ</foreign>, in which the middle letter is pronounced with a sound between that of <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> and that of <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, or resembling that of <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>. (IJ, TA.) As Er-Rághib says, <foreign lang="ar">سُؤَالٌ</foreign> signifies The <hi rend="ital">asking,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demanding, knowledge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">information,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">what leads thereto:</hi> and the <hi rend="ital">asking,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demanding, property,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">what leads thereto.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلْتُهُ عَنِ الشَّىْءِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">I asked of him information respecting the thing:</hi> (IB, TA: [and the like is said in the Msb:]) and <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلْتُهُ الشَّىْءَ</foreign> [is sometimes used in the same sense, as has been shown above, but generally] means <hi rend="ital">I asked him to give me the thing:</hi> (IB, TA:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَهُ مَالًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He asked, demanded, or begged, of him property,</hi> and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَ مِنْهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> [followed by <foreign lang="ar">مَالًا</foreign>]: (MA:) and <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلْتُ ٱللّٰهَ العَافِيَةَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سُؤَالٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسْأَلَةٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">I begged, or sought, of God health,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">freedom from disease,</hi> &amp;c. (Msb.) The saying in the Kur [lxx. 1], <foreign lang="ar">سَأَلَ سَائِلٌ بِعَذَابٍ وَاقِعٍ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَذَابٍ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">An asker asked respecting a falling punishment</hi>]: (S:) [for] one says, <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجْنَا نَسْأَلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِفُلَانٍ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">We went forth asking respecting such a one</hi>]: (Akh, S:) or the phrase in the Kur means <hi rend="ital">a caller called</hi> [<hi rend="ital">for a falling punishment</hi>]: (TA:) and some read <foreign lang="ar">سَالَ سَائِلٌ بعذاب واقع</foreign>, (Bd, TA,) [likewise] from <foreign lang="ar">السُّؤَالُ</foreign>: (Bd:) or this means <foreign lang="ar">سَالَ وَادٍ بعذاب واقع</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">a valley flowed with a falling punishment</hi>]; (Bd, TA;) so some say; (TA;) from <foreign lang="ar">السَّيَلَانُ</foreign>. (Bd.) The saying, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">نَهَى عَنْ كَثْرَةِ السَّؤَالِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He</hi> (Mohammad) <hi rend="ital">forbade much questioning</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inquiring</hi>] is said to relate to subtile questions or inquiries, that are needless; like another trad., mentioned below, voce, <foreign lang="ar">مَسْأَلَةٌ</foreign>: or to the begging, of men, their property needlessly.                      <L>

                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Didst thou ask the remains of the dwelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">didst thou not ask, respecting the inhabitants, or respecting their knowledge of the former occupants?</hi>]. (M, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  In the saying of Bilál Ibn-Jereer, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَجَدْتَ بِهِمْ عِلَّةً حَاضِرَهْ</foreign> 
                     </L>

                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا ضِفْتَهُمْ أَوْ سَآيَلْتَهُمْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">When thou becomest their guest, or askest of them, thou findest with them a ready excuse</hi>], <foreign lang="ar">سَآيَلْتَهُمْ</foreign> is a combination of two dial. vars.; the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> being in the original phrase <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَلْتُ زَيْدًا</foreign>, and the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> being a substitute in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">سَايَلْتُ زَيْدًا</foreign>; the measure of <foreign lang="ar">سَآيَلْتَهُمْ</foreign> being <foreign lang="ar">فَعَايَلْتَهُمْ</foreign>: (M, K: *) so said Ahmad Ibn-Yahyà, [i. e. Th,] who had at first ignored the expression: (M:) and it is an instance of which we know not a parallel in the language. (M, K. *)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Accord. to analogy, <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَلَهَ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He asked him, &amp;c., being asked by him,</hi> &amp;c.          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And Freytag states that Reiske has explained <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَلَ</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">He always demanded that another should express wishes for his health:</hi> but I know not any instance of its being used in this sense.]    </entryFree>27:T737,<entryFree id="n18581" key="تَسَآءَلُوا" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">They asked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">begged, one another.</hi> (S, Msb, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا يَتَسَآءَلَانِ</foreign>, (M,) and also <foreign lang="ar">يَتَسَاوَلَانِ</foreign>, (M, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">يَتَسَايَلَانِ</foreign>. (TA.) In the Kur [iv. 1], some read <foreign lang="ar">وَٱتَّقُوا ٱللّٰهَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱلَّذِى تَسَّآءَلُونَ بِهِ</foreign>; and others, <foreign lang="ar">تَسَآءَلُونَ بِهِ</foreign>: in each case, originally <foreign lang="ar">تَتَسَآءَلُونَ</foreign>: the meaning is, [<hi rend="ital">And fear ye God,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">by Whom ye demand</hi> [<hi rend="ital">one of another</hi>] <hi rend="ital">your rights,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dues:</hi> (M:) or <hi rend="ital">by Whom ye ask,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demand, one of another;</hi> (Bd, Jel;) <hi rend="ital">saying, I ask thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beg thee, by God;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">I beseech thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adjure thee, by God.</hi> (Jel.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  One says also <foreign lang="ar">تَسَآءَلُوا القَوْمَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">They</hi> [<hi rend="ital">together</hi>] <hi rend="ital">asked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">begged, the people.</hi> (Mgh in art. <foreign lang="ar">نقض</foreign>.)    </entryFree>28:Tb0a,<entryFree id="n18582" key="سُؤْلٌ" type="main">
